990,"The City of Anaheim denied a Conditional Use Permit for Grandma's House of Hope even though the house was an bedroom, sq ft house for homeless women suffering from serious and persistent mental illness.",0
991,This Is the email from the CEO at GHH:,N
992,"Blessings Collaborative Members,",1
993,"I am reaching out for assistance in a very important matter. Grandmaâ€™s House of Hope operates numerous shelter sites in Anaheim to serve vulnerable women with disabilities experiencing trauma of homelessness. We do so in residential neighborhoods coexisting peacefully with the neighbors and providing a home environment to our participants who need a safe space to heal. Whenever we have more than six individuals living in a house, we must apply to the City of Anaheim for a Conditional Use Permit (CUP) and supply information on the proposed project and target population. We have been successful in every application we have submitted in our year history and have ultimately won over even our most skeptical of neighbors.",1
994,"However, recently we applied for a CUP to operate an bedroom, sq ft house for homeless women suffering from serious and persistent mental illness who may or may not have developed a substance use disorder as a result. This was the first time we specified a target population of serving those with mental health diagnosis.",0
995,"Of note: The participants in this program have already been connected to a mental health clinic, diagnosed and given a treatment plan and referred to the OCHCA, who then assesses them for placement in our program. These participants are not required to come into our program and do this of their own free will, expressing their desire to receive services and WANT HELP to change their circumstances.",1
996,"The neighborhood banded together in a mob-like way during the Planning Commission meeting and spouted the most hateful and discriminatory speech you can imagine. The Planning Commission caved and denied our permit although the staff report had already addressed the issues brought up and found there to be no evidence that there would be an adverse impact on the surrounding neighbors. There was no effort made to ask if any of their concerns could be mitigated and overcome and when I offered to do so, I was shouted into silence by the crowd. The situation was so disturbing that the City Attorney for Anaheim also made a point to caution the commission that denying the permit could be considered as a violation of the Americas with Disabilities Act (ADA) and Housing Accountability Act (HAA).",0
997,"Needless to say, we are appealing this decision and will be going before the City Council to defend our project on October th at pm at Anaheim City Hall.
